When mucous membranes are expelled from the hip joint area and caused by its contents as well as local factors of their environment; this is called a prolapsed disc, where one hernia bulges out more over the other when compared to them. A common name for such condition used in practice is "slipped disk." (The term slipped or ruptured disk has been historically misleading because it implies that part of an intervertebral disc protrudes into and damages nearby nerve tissue, which rarely occurs.) The location where the hip dislocation is reduced in a supine position (lying face upward). This approach provides optimal access to perform reduction maneuvers with gravity assisting, aiming for minimal trauma

This technique emphasizes careful handling during reduction to minimize complications such as avascular necrosis or heterotopic ossification, which are serious potential consequences when mismanaged dislocations occur.
